  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_eaaabf3c-1432-4f9e-80c9-55843c35b094'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer7515613088377345852">Existing at the fringes of Washington D.C., the Club consists of four eccentric members. Led by a mysterious man know as "Oliver Stone," they study conspiracy theories, current events, and the machinations of government to discover the "truth" behind the country's actions. Their efforts bear little fruit --- until the group witnesses a shocking murder ... and become embroi</span>
  <span id="freeText7515613088377345852" style="display:none">Existing at the fringes of Washington D.C., the Club consists of four eccentric members. Led by a mysterious man know as "Oliver Stone," they study conspiracy theories, current events, and the machinations of government to discover the "truth" behind the country's actions. Their efforts bear little fruit --- until the group witnesses a shocking murder ... and become embroiled in an astounding, far reaching conspiracy. Now the Club must join forces with a Secret Service agent to confront one of the most chilling spectacles ever to take place on American soil --- an event that may trigger the ultimate war between two different worlds. And all that stands in the way of this apocalypse is five unexpected heroes.</span>

Stone says “Because camels have great stamina They never give up” Then Reuben says the real re<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">In Chapter 70 Alex asks why it’s called the Camel Club. Stone says “Because camels have great stamina They never give up” Then Reuben says the real reason is “In the 1920’s there was another Camel Club. And at each meeting of that club they would all raise their glasses and take a vow to oppose Prohibition to the last drop of Whiskey”<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8389810700668991049">Some people follow sports teams, other people follow actors or rock bands. But me, I follow authors. And while some people fantasize about celebrities they’d like to dine with, I have a list of rock star authors I dream of interviewing.<br/><br/>Recently, one of my dreams came true when David Baldacci agreed to an email interview with me. Upon hearing the news, my impulse was to jump and kick in a manner my legs haven’t experienced since the late 1980s, when I was a high school cheerleader. I quickly disc</span>
  <span id="freeText8389810700668991049" style="display:none">Some people follow sports teams, other people follow actors or rock bands. But me, I follow authors. And while some people fantasize about celebrities they’d like to dine with, I have a list of rock star authors I dream of interviewing.<br /><br />Recently, one of my dreams came true when David Baldacci agreed to an email interview with me. Upon hearing the news, my impulse was to jump and kick in a manner my legs haven’t experienced since the late 1980s, when I was a high school cheerleader. I quickly discovered my body is no longer qualified in jumping and kicking. It is, however, perfectly fine sitting at a computer conducting research on a favorite author. So that’s what I did. And here’s what I learned: <br /><br />Before becoming an internationally-acclaimed bestselling author, Baldacci practiced law for nine years. He hit success with his first novel, “Absolute Power” and hasn’t looked back. He’s written more than a dozen best sellers. Baldacci’s works are translated into more than 45 languages and sold in more than 80 countries. And over 60 million copies of Baldacci's books are in print worldwide.<br /><br />Even I, an ardent Baldacci fan, was surprised by those statistics. And if I wasn’t a fan, upon learning those stats, I’d feel inclined to read a Baldacci title.<br /><br />A good place to start is with Baldacci’s “The Camel Club.” This book is the first in a series which follows a club of D.C.-based truth seekers. The club consists of an unusual mix of four members: a man without a past currently called "Oliver Stone"; obsessive computer genius Milton Farb; blue-collar laborer Reuben Rhodes; and Library of Congress reference specialist Caleb Shaw. <br /><br />In “The Camel Club,” the members witness a shocking murder in a D.C.-area park. While secretly trying to unravel the crime, the foursome is slammed into a plot that threatens national security and world stability. <br /><br />If that’s not enough to get you reading Baldacci, perhaps a taste of my interview will do it. (The full interview is available on my blog, address below.)<br /><br />Question: An enormous amount of research must go into your writing. Is there a particular research experience or discovery you’ll always remember? <br /><br />Answer: Listening to incessant gunfire at Quantico while I was down there researching “Last Man Standing.” I felt like I was in the Middle East. Being nearly arrested by the FBI while toting around a German film crew in D.C. Ranks right up there. And then my experience on the Acela train after two passengers overheard me talking to a medical expert about poisoning someone for research for a book and summoned the police. That was fun too. Now whenever I travel, I duct tape my mouth shut just to be safe. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8389810700668991049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2121218335" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2121218335" />
    <a title="Rita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22264452-rita"><img alt="Rita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598724761p2/22264452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2121218335?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rita" href="/user/show/22264452-rita">Rita</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781616852436" href="/book/show/8196697-the-camel-club">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22264452-rita?shelf=espionage">espionage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22264452-rita?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22264452-rita?shelf=political">political</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22264452-rita?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2121218335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11403908603505416411">Since I'm feeling better, I decided it was about time to write the review for this fantastic book. The only other David Baldacci book that I had read was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15159.Absolute_Power' title='Absolute Power by David Baldacci' rel='nofollow noopener'>Absolute Power</a> which I enjoyed very much but it was quite a few years ago. I decided to find out what all the fuss was about this author. The next one I tried was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11007587.Zero_Day__John_Puller___1_' title='Zero Day (John Puller, #1) by David Baldacci' rel='nofollow noopener'>Zero Day</a>. I ended up throwing that one in the DNF file. The lead character, John Puller, completely left me cold. He struck me as a cardboard caricature of a military lifer would be b</span>
  <span id="freeText11403908603505416411" style="display:none">Since I'm feeling better, I decided it was about time to write the review for this fantastic book. The only other David Baldacci book that I had read was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15159.Absolute_Power" title="Absolute Power by David Baldacci" rel="nofollow noopener">Absolute Power</a> which I enjoyed very much but it was quite a few years ago. I decided to find out what all the fuss was about this author. The next one I tried was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11007587.Zero_Day__John_Puller___1_" title="Zero Day (John Puller, #1) by David Baldacci" rel="nofollow noopener">Zero Day</a>. I ended up throwing that one in the DNF file. The lead character, John Puller, completely left me cold. He struck me as a cardboard caricature of a military lifer would be but with no emotions. Definitely not a Jack Reacher. So on to the next one.<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15158.The_Camel_Club__Camel_Club___1_" title="The Camel Club (Camel Club, #1) by David Baldacci" rel="nofollow noopener">The Camel Club</a> was a breath of fresh air after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11007587.Zero_Day__John_Puller___1_" title="Zero Day (John Puller, #1) by David Baldacci" rel="nofollow noopener">Zero Day</a>. "Oliver Stone" was a man who had been to hell and back and still cared about wrongs being done to people and his country. Despite the fact that an agency of the American government took away everything he held precious in his life, Oliver Stone still loved his country and was willing to do everything in his power to protect it. I was hooked.<br />Milton Farb, Caleb Shaw and Reuben Rhodes comprised the remainder of "the Camel Club" with long term Secret Service Agent, Alex Ford, an unofficial member. They are conspiracy theorists who discovered the truth behind the theories. They know all too well that government agencies sometimes crossed lines that shouldn't be crossed.<br />It starts with them witnessing a murder that is not just a murder. The victim was killed to make sure that something that is happening at the most powerful government agency and shouldn't be, is kept quiet. But Oliver and the rest of the Camel Club are detected in their wooden boat, and a hail of bullets put a hole in the boat and grazes one of the club members.<br />Oliver Stone convinces Agent Ford to look into the matter and he ends up being demoted back to White House protection detail for his trouble. He stepped on toes that did not like being stepped on and were in a powerful position to get back at him for his audacity.<br />The real point of this book, I believe, is that it is very easy for a person who believes he is a force for good to be manipulated by those who do not have good intentions. Believing that it's OK to overstep boundaries because of the greater good, will usually not work as planned. You are putting yourself in the position of being an omnipotent being while in fact you are only a human being. You mean no harm but that is usually what you get. So it seems that at times the worst enemy of the USA can be one of the bureaucracies put in place to protect it, simply because the person in charge thinks that they know what is best for the country.<br />I really enjoyed this book and look forward to the rest of this series. I'm glad that I gave David Baldacci another chance.<br />Posted to Goodreads and Amazon 1/20/2018</span>
  <a data-text-id="11403908603505416411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_964604263" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/964604263" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/964604263?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781616852436" href="/book/show/8196697-the-camel-club">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer964604263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7902525394375009729"><b>Updating just to correct some typos and grammatical problems. </b> <br/><br/><br/>Well....here I go. I can't really recommend this one. You know there are books by Mr. Baldacci that I enjoy greatly. I have noted before that he can be...that's "can be" one of those authors who can get very heavy handed about their political beliefs. <br/><br/>I find that the case here. He pretty much had me feeling he was really (really) <b>mostly</b> interested in making a political point. This is obviously a point to be agreed or disagreed on as </span>
  <span id="freeText7902525394375009729" style="display:none"><b>Updating just to correct some typos and grammatical problems. </b> <br /><br /><br />Well....here I go. I can't really recommend this one. You know there are books by Mr. Baldacci that I enjoy greatly. I have noted before that he can be...that's "can be" one of those authors who can get very heavy handed about their political beliefs. <br /><br />I find that the case here. He pretty much had me feeling he was really (really) <b>mostly</b> interested in making a political point. This is obviously a point to be agreed or disagreed on as I see some reviewers agree with me and others don't. Possibly it depends on how much you agree with him (Baldacci) and therefore how much that part of the book...sticks out or overwhelms the plot and characters. I don't know. You'll have to decide for yourself.<br /><br />Now that said, this is not the primary problem with the novel for me and it's not why I give it a low rating. The novel starts out with an idea and a cast of characters we are to get to know. The primary protagonist is <i>Oliver Stone</i>. No not the movie maker. We have another refugee from the world of secret, black ops, covert...stuff. His having taken the name of the movie maker who's interest in conspiracies is sort of legend may just have been part of the reason why the name was chosen as our hero's nom de plume. Sadly however from the very first things spin out in several directions and the story gets not so much laid out with lots of threads...as it seems to fray out in all directions with the threads lashing about in the wind.<br /><br />It wasn't that I couldn't keep track...I just came to the point where I didn't care to.<br /><br />So, I don't plan to follow up with any more of the series and really can't recommend it. I just found myself too often losing interest and wanting to move on to something...interesting. <br /><br />Oh and as I and others have said, Mr. Baldacci's politics quickly become the only true point.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7902525394375009729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_112481172" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112481172" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112481172?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=x-filing-and-secret-histories">x-filing-and-secret-histories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2000-2005">2000-2005</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=spy-stuff">spy-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112481172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8005322625275095975">2.0 stars. Probably would have given this 3 stars except for my extreme annoyance with the "heavy handed" political tone of the book. As far as I can tell from the authors depictions in the story, America is responsible for ALL of the evil in the world (especially in the Middle East), 9/11 was a justified response to American foreign policy and Americans are ignorant and racist. Great, thanks for that, now can we get on with the story. Oh, that is the story. Terrific!!!<br/><br/>Apart from the tone, this </span>
  <span id="freeText8005322625275095975" style="display:none">2.0 stars. Probably would have given this 3 stars except for my extreme annoyance with the "heavy handed" political tone of the book. As far as I can tell from the authors depictions in the story, America is responsible for ALL of the evil in the world (especially in the Middle East), 9/11 was a justified response to American foreign policy and Americans are ignorant and racist. Great, thanks for that, now can we get on with the story. Oh, that is the story. Terrific!!!<br /><br />Apart from the tone, this was a fairly fast-paced read with competent writing. I may check out the next book in the series at some point as I thought the basic premise of the Camel Club was intriguing. I just hope the author focuses more on story-telling and less on rhetoric in future books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8005322625275095975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1217140990" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1217140990" />
    <a title="Freda Malone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6938113-freda-malone"><img alt="Freda Malone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418039583p2/6938113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1217140990?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Freda Malone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Freda Malone" href="/user/show/6938113-freda-malone">Freda Malone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1217140990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13381726991430924594">Across the street from the White House, tells a story of a man, dead and alive, Oliver Stone. Old and homeless, he and a small group of friends known as The Camel Club, witness a murder on Roosevelt Island. <br/> <br/>I read this book many years ago, but for the life of me, I could not remember very much of it. Except for the fact that Oliver Stone lived homeless across the street from the White house and was a mysterious old man. Now that I have re-read this first novel in the series, scenes and characte</span>
  <span id="freeText13381726991430924594" style="display:none">Across the street from the White House, tells a story of a man, dead and alive, Oliver Stone. Old and homeless, he and a small group of friends known as The Camel Club, witness a murder on Roosevelt Island. <br /> <br />I read this book many years ago, but for the life of me, I could not remember very much of it. Except for the fact that Oliver Stone lived homeless across the street from the White house and was a mysterious old man. Now that I have re-read this first novel in the series, scenes and characters have come back to me, though I had to finish the book because I still couldn’t remember the ending! Explosive, to say the least and so many characters involved, you really have to pay attention.<br /> <br />A topic that stands out in this novel is the amount of veteran characters who were betrayed by their own government and the people high up in it. The president is a pompous ass who loves the cameras and doesn’t seem to care much for ‘the people’, just his looks and his image. Carter Gray, the nation's intelligence chief, struck me as some kind of snake and had his own agenda and I wasn’t wrong about that in the end. Alex, a CIA agent, gets a rookie partner, Jackie Simpson, who is also the daughter of a Senator. Jackie Simpson should never have transferred from beat cop to CIA, she was dumb as a door nail and I really didn’t like her. She was like an annoying fly buzzing around your head and wouldn’t figure things out on her own. Then of course we have a few CIA characters who were corrupt, some deranged Muslims, and some Korean ninjas. <br /> <br />The conspiracy itself was creative and well thought out. As always with the government, things aren’t what they seem. The Camel Club characters were memorable, mainly because of their atypical personalities and behaviors. Hard to picture a few old men trying to save the world though. We find out who Oliver Stone really is and he is interesting enough to continue reading the rest of the series, because my first question is, where did Oliver Stone come from? All we know in this first novel is that Oliver Stone is a force to be reckoned with and I want to read more.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13381726991430924594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3544287399682123710">I'm just blabbering about this read:<br/><br/> - how insignificant we are. Why fight/appose/criticize/object to anything when we're simply not important? Depressing;<br/><br/>- some Americans will approve of the criticism in the book, other will be furious and frustrated;<br/><br/>- this book proves a point. How democracy is used as a weapon to control countries, a well done and straightforward explanation; sadly true as well;<br/><br/>- a cliffhanger ending; don't want to indulge in the series, so I'm unhappy;<br/><br/>- I liked, as in really </span>
  <span id="freeText3544287399682123710" style="display:none">I'm just blabbering about this read:<br /><br /> - how insignificant we are. Why fight/appose/criticize/object to anything when we're simply not important? Depressing;<br /><br />- some Americans will approve of the criticism in the book, other will be furious and frustrated;<br /><br />- this book proves a point. How democracy is used as a weapon to control countries, a well done and straightforward explanation; sadly true as well;<br /><br />- a cliffhanger ending; don't want to indulge in the series, so I'm unhappy;<br /><br />- I liked, as in really liked, the big <i>WHAT IF</i> scenario in the book, not preposterous at all;<br /><br />- a political plot with eccentric interesting anti-hero, conspiracy theorist characters. A spy thriller with the usual James Bond, over the top, plot. Robert Ludlum, Tom Clancy, Fredrick Forsyth, John Le Carré fans will love this book.<br /><br />- there's a confusing 'message' in the book. Should Americans be proud of their weaponry? Sure. Should they be proud of the reason why they need it? uhummmm...if I was an American, I would be scared to death, instead. An angry world is an ugly enemy - is my humble opinion.<br /><br />Everything is too predictable. We've seen these kind of heroes in too many self-soothing/ self-congratulatory, slap-on-the-back kind of books. I'll go for four stars, but actually would have liked 3.5. <br /><br />Anyway, the book stirs thought, and that's a good thing. So I will stick to the four stars and be done with it.</span>

    <a title="Jonetta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4876540-jonetta"><img alt="Jonetta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329083158p2/4876540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/277152471?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonetta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonetta" href="/user/show/4876540-jonetta">Jonetta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780759515239" href="/book/show/9920129-the-camel-club">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer277152471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12696392271435733404">The Camel Club is comprised of a group of men who are sort of a counter culture of their own after having served the country in some form or fashion, enough to be suspicious of the publicly fed information from the government. They lead an odd existence, each with unique quirks and eccentricities, and meet each month to compare notes on what they're hearing from various inside sources. On one of these evenings, they unfortunately become witnesses to a stunning event that puts them in the middle </span>
  <span id="freeText12696392271435733404" style="display:none">The Camel Club is comprised of a group of men who are sort of a counter culture of their own after having served the country in some form or fashion, enough to be suspicious of the publicly fed information from the government. They lead an odd existence, each with unique quirks and eccentricities, and meet each month to compare notes on what they're hearing from various inside sources. On one of these evenings, they unfortunately become witnesses to a stunning event that puts them in the middle of a situation that threatens the safety of the country and the world. <br /><br />There are several stories going on here that ultimately converge, which is an approach I happen to love for this genre. While it presents a challenge to keep up with all the characters, it certainly heightens the mystery, suspense and intrigue. There are quite a few twists and surprises that make it even better, ultimately leading to a pretty exciting climax, though I had some issues with some things in the ending. Political perspectives are also rampant with multiple points of view to keep it provacative. <br /><br />I highly recommend this book and plan to continue the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12696392271435733404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2321877149" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12482393914133477360">Read the review of the entire Camel Club series at my <a href='https://wp.me/p9nt3E-uS' rel='nofollow noopener'>my blog</a><br/><br/>The Camel Club has an interesting premise in the action thriller genre. It consists of four washed up, eccentric senior gentlemen who want to make the world a better place. This premise intrigued me and made me pick up this book. <br/><br/>Now, I have read Baldacci's Will Robie before and I liked that series. The review of the series is available <a href='https://digitalamrit.com/2018/02/11/review-of-the-will-robie-series-by-david-baldacci/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>. The Camel Club is different since it does not rely on one individual to move the plot along th</span>
  <span id="freeText12482393914133477360" style="display:none">Read the review of the entire Camel Club series at my <a href="https://wp.me/p9nt3E-uS" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a><br /><br />The Camel Club has an interesting premise in the action thriller genre. It consists of four washed up, eccentric senior gentlemen who want to make the world a better place. This premise intrigued me and made me pick up this book. <br /><br />Now, I have read Baldacci's Will Robie before and I liked that series. The review of the series is available <a href="https://digitalamrit.com/2018/02/11/review-of-the-will-robie-series-by-david-baldacci/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>. The Camel Club is different since it does not rely on one individual to move the plot along though some members of the club are more equal than the others. This book takes the standard islamic terror plot and gives it an interesting twist. For the most part, the US is portrayed more as sinners than as being sinned against. The outlook here is far more international than I would have expected, which is good in a way. As a result, all the characters are interesting - both the protagonists and antagonists.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12482393914133477360" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer269829294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8914290134999459356"><br/><br/>How wrong can you be. This started ok. I wondered why the treatise on the nature of Islam, was prepared to accept that somehow the relevance of that would make itself apparent.<br/>Wrong again <br/><br/>20% read and starting to find it tiresome, but this was an author recommended by a friend so I ploughed on. <br/><br/>What a lot of characters and acronyms and superheros and who the hell is this book written for? Seems to me the target audience is an adolescent youth the author is hoping to 'educate' Yet I'm thinking it</span>
  <span id="freeText8914290134999459356" style="display:none"><br /><br />How wrong can you be. This started ok. I wondered why the treatise on the nature of Islam, was prepared to accept that somehow the relevance of that would make itself apparent.<br />Wrong again <br /><br />20% read and starting to find it tiresome, but this was an author recommended by a friend so I ploughed on. <br /><br />What a lot of characters and acronyms and superheros and who the hell is this book written for? Seems to me the target audience is an adolescent youth the author is hoping to 'educate' Yet I'm thinking it more a 'Mills &amp; Boon for boys. I never thought I'd ever see "educate" and Mills &amp; Boon in the same paragraph, but there you go. <br /><br />The fact that I think this book has a target audience doesn't go down well with me. A book written specifically to sell rather than an outlet for the tale needing to be told.<br /><br />By the time I had managed to get 50% read I really couldn't take any more. <br />I really didn't like all the extra information - seemed to me the author was trying to prove he'd done some research. Not impressed - he may have read a few things but I never got the impression that he really understood the 'research' he'd done, he merely wanted to impress the reader. Didn't work - not impressed.<br /><br />A book gratefully abandoned. I have to admit there were some bits I liked ... but not many. If I was desperate to read something and no other options I might read this to the end. <br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151900415?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mish" href="/user/show/5071350-mish">Mish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151900415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17685646199270264629">Extremely bad<br/><br/>I read this book because it was chosen by my book club - I don't think I would have bothered to finish it otherwise.<br/><br/>The plot is ridiculous and lunges around especially towards the end - it felt like a badly written James Bond movie. The nuclear strike was averted by just 1 second - that sort of timing is not dramatic - it's just annoying. <br/><br/>The characterisation was quite two dimensional and, in the case of Hemingway, quite nauseating - his accomplishments are just too unbelievable - s</span>
  <span id="freeText17685646199270264629" style="display:none">Extremely bad<br /><br />I read this book because it was chosen by my book club - I don't think I would have bothered to finish it otherwise.<br /><br />The plot is ridiculous and lunges around especially towards the end - it felt like a badly written James Bond movie. The nuclear strike was averted by just 1 second - that sort of timing is not dramatic - it's just annoying. <br /><br />The characterisation was quite two dimensional and, in the case of Hemingway, quite nauseating - his accomplishments are just too unbelievable - standing on a 1 inch ledge in a gale force wind for 6 hours and being able to kill people with your fingers? Hai-ya!<br /><br />I don't think these extremes are necessary to make an interesting character or story and the use of them just makes the book seem ridiculous.<br /><br />I also found the writing very clunky and badly phrased. Some of the dialogue perhaps is accurate for the characters but the same inarticulate leaden style is in the narrative - I just found it to be very naive.<br /><br />As for the educational aspects - I found that, at times, patronising. Worse though is that it spoiled the continuity of the writing. Perhaps if the elements were less convoluted then it may have made the going a bit easier? I really don't want to wade through so much instruction whilst reading escapist fiction.<br /><br />On the whole I thought it was very poor and I would encourage anyone else to leave it well alone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17685646199270264629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas"><img alt="Benjamin Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451660582p2/4209082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1881554978?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin Thomas" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas">Benjamin Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=thriller-political">thriller-political</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=thriller-cops-feds">thriller-cops-feds</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1881554978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16526189292337137537">Four societal misfits and conspiracy theorists living in the Washington DC area have banded together to form what they refer to as the Camel Club. Led by Oliver Stone, a 60+ year old man with a mysterious past, they find themselves accidentally witnessing a murder. That launches them into an adventure beyond their wildest expectations involving a complex and bizarre terrorist plot.<br/><br/>I’ve been a David Baldacci fan since I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15159.Absolute_Power' title='Absolute Power by David Baldacci' rel='nofollow noopener'>Absolute Power</a>. His books don’t always quite live up to that one in my m</span>
  <span id="freeText16526189292337137537" style="display:none">Four societal misfits and conspiracy theorists living in the Washington DC area have banded together to form what they refer to as the Camel Club. Led by Oliver Stone, a 60+ year old man with a mysterious past, they find themselves accidentally witnessing a murder. That launches them into an adventure beyond their wildest expectations involving a complex and bizarre terrorist plot.<br /><br />I’ve been a David Baldacci fan since I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15159.Absolute_Power" title="Absolute Power by David Baldacci" rel="nofollow noopener">Absolute Power</a>. His books don’t always quite live up to that one in my mind but I can pretty much guarantee a good read. To be honest, I wasn’t expecting as much from this one due to some less-than-positive- reviews from my Goodreads friends whose opinions I greatly respect. But I will say now that I enjoyed this one quite a lot. The characters were engaging, not only the four members of the Camel Club but the Secret Service, the terrorists, and even the politicians. The plot required some suspension of disbelief but was nevertheless interesting and moved along swiftly. Most of the novel ticked along fairly predictably but it was evident that something else was unfolding that I needed to be patient for. The payoff was worth it as the nature of the terrorist plot turned out to be anything but predictable and was one of the most unusual I have yet read.<br /><br />Looking forward to reading the rest of this series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16526189292337137537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2352836753" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2352836753" />
    <a title="David Highton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48750300-david-highton"><img alt="David Highton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598679306p2/48750300.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2352836753?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Highton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Highton" href="/user/show/48750300-david-highton">David Highton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780330441230" href="/book/show/820580.The_Camel_Club">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2352836753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2712694297620897422">An introduction to the Camel Club, a group of conspiracy theorists led by the mysterious Oliver Stone who see a murder and get led into a major attempt against the US president. A monster book nearly 700 pages and I found the first 150-200 pages very slow in the set-up to the main story</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5821727591249933952" style="display:none">The Camel Club - a rag tag team of friends led by the "past-less" Oliver Stone - is a strangely capable group who's purpose is to discover the truth about what's really going on in the government. When they stumbles upon a murder that smells of corruption - it becomes a lethal race to discover the murderers' identities and silence them before the Camel Club is the one to get silenced.<br /><br />The Camel Club combines mystery, suspense, and action in a moderately paced adult read. Readers should be aware that it contains non-graphic killing (references to blood and method of death), profanity, sexual banter, and numerous debates of Islamic and Western cultures. <br /><br />Although The Camel Club is the first book in a series, it can be treated as a stand alone book.<br /><br />See this and more content based reviews at <a href="http://ssbookreviews.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah's Reviews</a></span>

<div id="review_2375479430" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2375479430" />
    <a title="Vignesh Ashok Kumar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33449035-vignesh-ashok-kumar"><img alt="Vignesh Ashok Kumar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547524025p2/33449035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2375479430?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vignesh Ashok Kumar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vignesh Ashok Kumar" href="/user/show/33449035-vignesh-ashok-kumar">Vignesh Ashok Kumar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33449035-vignesh-ashok-kumar?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33449035-vignesh-ashok-kumar?shelf=espionage">espionage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33449035-vignesh-ashok-kumar?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2375479430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7778598310601737945"><b> Rating - 6/10(Okay) - Rip-off of White House Down!! :( </b> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1545992174i/26822056.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>After reading the Camel Club series as a whole, the order of the books from better to worst is - <br/><i> #5 > #4 > #2 > #3 >#1 </i><br/><br/>After reading the synopsis of what the book will be about, I was thrilled. But I learned the hard way that not to judge the book by it's cover. The book, as the title suggests, is <b> The Camel Club </b>. It should revolve mostly around The Camel Club right? But this book gives us the impression that it will be based on them but</span>
  <span id="freeText7778598310601737945" style="display:none"><b> Rating - 6/10(Okay) - Rip-off of White House Down!! :( </b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1545992174i/26822056.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After reading the Camel Club series as a whole, the order of the books from better to worst is - <br><i> #5 &gt; #4 &gt; #2 &gt; #3 &gt;#1 </i><br><br>After reading the synopsis of what the book will be about, I was thrilled. But I learned the hard way that not to judge the book by it's cover. The book, as the title suggests, is <b> The Camel Club </b>. It should revolve mostly around The Camel Club right? But this book gives us the impression that it will be based on them but throws stones at us by having them only in lesser part of the novel( I don't remember exactly the fraction). The book should have been named as <b> The Revenge of the Arabs </b> or <b> White House Down... Not Again!!! </b><br><br>Oh man!!! That is some accusation. I am not going to go straight ahead and say not to read the book. The book is about a conspiracy plot(which IMO is not that much of a conspiracy, one would also think so) involving kidnapping of the president for god knows what until, you know, The Camel Club saves the day by a slim chance. Yeay!! The intention of this was also not that great. There were also many plot holes I thought should be resolved. The book also made me think that I wasn't supposed to ask how this particular person knows so and so things.<br><br>But apart from, the book stood strong in terms of the characters. The characters were the main reason I read the book till the end. The life and struggle the characters face in the world of chaos was portrayed beautifully. I loved the chemistry between the characters. The book also made me cry at the end. The pain of loosing one's daughter without knowing that it is one's daughter was the sad part of this entire novel. The book also rained on facts regarding American history, life, culture and how it affects other countries. The action scenes were completely terrific(prologue is my most favorite). <br><br>I would give this book 3.8 stars. I wanted to give this book 5 but due to these factors I had to lower the score. My suggestion is that the author should spend equal amounts in crafting a story well deserved to it's name and also on current affairs. I hope that it gets better as I read the sequels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7778598310601737945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The Camel Club is a group of people led by presumed deceased John Carr who is now known as Oliver Stone, and they witness the murder of a man, and they are the only ones who witness it, they are now trying to discover the truth behind the murder.<br /><br />Now that I've read the first book in the series, I plan on reading the other books as well.</span>

<div id="review_2407019572" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2407019572" />
    <a title="Tina Woodbury" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5859754-tina-woodbury"><img alt="Tina Woodbury" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494643405p2/5859754.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2407019572?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina Woodbury" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina Woodbury" href="/user/show/5859754-tina-woodbury">Tina Woodbury</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780446577380" href="/book/show/823653.The_Camel_Club">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2407019572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9812859591464222836">For all of my reviews: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.readingbetweenthepagesblog.wordpress.com'>www.readingbetweenthepagesblog.wordpr...</a><br/><br/>** 3.5 Stars<br/>The Camel Club is a corky group of misfits. They are four members – Oliver Stone, Caleb Shaw, Reuben Rhodes, and Milton Farb. They are the eyes and ears of Washington, D.C. They lurk about where no one realizes they are being watched and listened to. This conspiracy theory group meets at night so they can go undetected all in the name of justice.<br/><br/>The Camel Club is in the wrong place at the wrong time and find themselves wi</span>
  <span id="freeText9812859591464222836" style="display:none">For all of my reviews: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.readingbetweenthepagesblog.wordpress.com">www.readingbetweenthepagesblog.wordpr...</a><br /><br />** 3.5 Stars<br />The Camel Club is a corky group of misfits. They are four members – Oliver Stone, Caleb Shaw, Reuben Rhodes, and Milton Farb. They are the eyes and ears of Washington, D.C. They lurk about where no one realizes they are being watched and listened to. This conspiracy theory group meets at night so they can go undetected all in the name of justice.<br /><br />The Camel Club is in the wrong place at the wrong time and find themselves witnesses of a murder. I really enjoyed the murder mystery storyline and all the characters involved in it. On the flip-side this book is very heavy-handed with politics, religion, terrorism, and the military. Of course when all is said and done it all ties in together, but getting there dragged on at times.<br /><br />There are a lot of characters in this book, therefore a lot of storylines to keep track of. The character development was done really well and added greatly to this multilayered book.<br /><br />The ending of this book was fantastic! It was intense, fast-paced, and captivating!<br /><br />I found the members of the Camel Club to be very intriguing. They all have very interesting and unique backgrounds that I look forward to seeing David Baldacci explore more as this series continues. I think there is a lot of potential in these characters and I am excited to move onto book two very soon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9812859591464222836" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

After witnessing a shocking murder, the Club is slammed headfirst into a plot that threatens the very security of the nation, full of stunning twists, high-stakes intrigue, and global gamesmanship rocketing to the Oval Office and beyond."</span>

<div id="review_1318878139" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1318878139" />
    <a title="Alcatraz Dey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30489708-alcatraz-dey"><img alt="Alcatraz Dey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540204089p2/30489708.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1318878139?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alcatraz Dey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alcatraz Dey" href="/user/show/30489708-alcatraz-dey">Alcatraz Dey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1318878139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17082170682217851912">The Camel Club is a political thriller that opens in Washington, D.C. (well, not quite. The opening chapter is not in D.C.), where we meet four eccentric, once-upon-a-time effective fellows who make up a group they call The Camel Club. Each has some kind of experience and/or brilliance that makes him essential to the small assembly; and each has been successful at one time or another in his life. Now, they are only reflections of what they once were. There's Oliver Stone (his assumed name), Cale</span>
  <span id="freeText17082170682217851912" style="display:none">The Camel Club is a political thriller that opens in Washington, D.C. (well, not quite. The opening chapter is not in D.C.), where we meet four eccentric, once-upon-a-time effective fellows who make up a group they call The Camel Club. Each has some kind of experience and/or brilliance that makes him essential to the small assembly; and each has been successful at one time or another in his life. Now, they are only reflections of what they once were. There's Oliver Stone (his assumed name), Caleb Shaw, Reuben Rhodes, and Milton Farb, conspiracy theorists all. They meet once a month in the middle of the night to discuss recent conspiracy theories and reflect/update those they've held for years. There are other interesting characters introduced in the early pages, including Secret Service agent Alex Ford who's on the downside of his career, and Kate Adams, a Department of Justice lawyer who works as a bartender at night. Go figure that one out! We are also briefly introduced to U.S. President, James H. Brennan, and to National Intelligence Center Director, Carter Gray, among others.<br /><br />Stone has a tent near the White House where he watches what goes on there. His goal is to find out the "truth" of things. He believes the American people have been denied that most desirous of tenets. On the evening of the beginning of this story, the Camel Club meets as arranged, but in the course of their meeting they unwittingly see a terrible crime committed on Theodore Roosevelt Island. Now, they must decide what to do about it...and I'm only on page 70! More later.<br /><br />October 29, 2005: It's later. Life sometimes gets in the way of finishing a good book, but it's been worth three nights up too late to do it in this case.<br /><br />The Camel Club members find themselves in the middle of a mess, having witnessed the murder of a Secret Service agent. Another Secret Service agent, Alex Ford, angers his superiors by deciding to investigate the death further than they had planned for this intended puppet. Stone and Ford end up working together to find out what's going on as a myriad of characters come and go, some with nefarious plans up their sleeves (there may even be a traitor in the club). It seems there are traitors everywhere and it's one of those times when one doesn't know who to trust. If you are into political intrigue, conspiracy theories, espionage, terrorism and/or assassination plots and all-around political paranoia, you will love this book. It is also very clearly and very well written. I can only say I hope there are many more Stones and Fords around than Captain Jacks and, well, others.<br /><br />Give yourself plenty of time to read The Camel Club. There are several subplots and lots of interesting facts about many things included in the story. The primary plot is very intense and you won't want to find yourself forgetting pertinent details leading up to the "game." It's enough to make the reader want to bolt the door and never leave home. I'm just glad it's fiction!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17082170682217851912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68202123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13509161789586233085">Awful. Hated 95% of the story, characters were not developed well, let alone new characters were still being added 50 pages from the end of the book. I didn't even care about the ones already present. <br/><br/>It seems that the author is trying way too hard to create a gripping, thrill-a-minute novel when in reality, the story is way too long and overtold. Many times while reading it, I felt like I was browsing wikipedia as many random facts were mentioned. I'm not sure if the author assumes his audience</span>
  <span id="freeText13509161789586233085" style="display:none">Awful. Hated 95% of the story, characters were not developed well, let alone new characters were still being added 50 pages from the end of the book. I didn't even care about the ones already present. <br /><br />It seems that the author is trying way too hard to create a gripping, thrill-a-minute novel when in reality, the story is way too long and overtold. Many times while reading it, I felt like I was browsing wikipedia as many random facts were mentioned. I'm not sure if the author assumes his audience is dumb or that he is pretentious enough that he feels the need to explain everything. Was I to be impressed with the extensive knowledge presented. I could hardly keep up with the acronyms and oh, by the way, this happened too... storytelling. Other sections of the book feel as if one is reading a newspaper account of the events. Too many times, items are repeated by different characters. One can only assume that either the author wasn't aware or that pure word count was at play. <br /><br />I've been told that his other books are better by several other people. I sure hope so as I picked up a few at a book sale. Hope my dollar wasn't wasted!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13509161789586233085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70983025-jack-heath?shelf=category-h-thriller">category-h-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2295149553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4057770618490115624">5 Stars. Enjoyable. We watch a conspiracy coming to light through two perspectives. First through our own eyes. We see some things happening independent of the second set of eyes, those of the four members of the Camel Club. I am still uncertain of the reason for that name, but they are a group of fringe eccentrics in the Washington area led by "Oliver Stone." The club's purpose? To ferret out conspiracies against the American government. A murder occurs and the repercussions slowly become appar</span>
  <span id="freeText4057770618490115624" style="display:none">5 Stars. Enjoyable. We watch a conspiracy coming to light through two perspectives. First through our own eyes. We see some things happening independent of the second set of eyes, those of the four members of the Camel Club. I am still uncertain of the reason for that name, but they are a group of fringe eccentrics in the Washington area led by "Oliver Stone." The club's purpose? To ferret out conspiracies against the American government. A murder occurs and the repercussions slowly become apparent. Stone himself is a mystery; has he been involved in these types of situations in the past? The group watch the comings and goings of the President and his chief advisers, trying to develop a cohesive story from short strings of information. They are assisted by Secret Service Agent Alex Ford who may not be totally aware of his role but, since he is on the brink of being fired, has nowhere else to turn. A wonderful first start for a continuing series. (October 2018)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4057770618490115624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2546115249" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2546115249" />
    <a title="Inqiad Ali" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/85763367-inqiad-ali"><img alt="Inqiad Ali" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2546115249?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Inqiad Ali" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Inqiad Ali" href="/user/show/85763367-inqiad-ali">Inqiad Ali</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2546115249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16972687149888271303">5 solid and thrilling stars.<br/>In the first book of the Camel Club series, we get introduced to the Camel Club, a group of conspiracy theorists whose aim is to uncover corruption in the upper reaches of the US government. This group is headed by Oliver Stone, whose real name is John Carr and who was a former CIA assassin. The Other members are Reuben Rhodes, a former military spy, Caleb Shaw, who works in the Library of Congress and Milton Farb, who was a child prodigy and now a web designer.<br/>The Bo</span>
  <span id="freeText16972687149888271303" style="display:none">5 solid and thrilling stars.<br />In the first book of the Camel Club series, we get introduced to the Camel Club, a group of conspiracy theorists whose aim is to uncover corruption in the upper reaches of the US government. This group is headed by Oliver Stone, whose real name is John Carr and who was a former CIA assassin. The Other members are Reuben Rhodes, a former military spy, Caleb Shaw, who works in the Library of Congress and Milton Farb, who was a child prodigy and now a web designer.<br />The Book gets started with three terrorists- Adnan al-Rimi, Mohammad al-Zawahiri and Gul Khan driving through the Interstate Highway near Virginia. A chopper then comes after their car and they flee inside the forests, where Adnan kills the latter two and places his lookalikes dead body with them. Then he enters the chopper and goes away.<br />Next, The Camel Club members accidentally witness the murder of Patrick Johnson, who was a data analyst in the National Intelligence Centre. He had been corrupting the files in the database on the orders of Tom Hemingway, one of the top most advisers Carter Gray, the intelligence chief. <br />The authorities were intent on writing it off as suicide, which was fuelled by the discovery of heroin in his lavish house. But the Camel Club, with the help of Secret Service Agent Alex Ford, started a more deeper and thorough investigation. For was assisted by Jackie Simpson, who is actually Carr's daughter. <br />For got kicked out of the investigation for his views and places on the presidential protection detail. The US president, James Brennan, was scheduled to go to his native town in Pennsylvania, which had renamed it self in honour of the local boy. But there on the dedication grounds, he was kidnapped by Adnan and other supposedly dead terrorists, and the world went to a complete meltdown. Tom Hemingway had orchestrated this and planned to return the president safely, but his plan was upset by Captain Jack, another former CIA assassin who had trained the terrorists. After much drama and a saga which almost lead to World War III, the president was finally rescued. The main events of the story shall remain untold, or else i would have to turn on the spoiler alert.<br />Overall, the book was fantastic and one of the best that i ever read. This book is highly recommended on your to read list.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16972687149888271303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_74130006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74130006" />
    <a title="BJ Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2030200-bj-rose"><img alt="BJ Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1237763983p2/2030200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74130006?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BJ Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BJ Rose" href="/user/show/2030200-bj-rose">BJ Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to BJ Rose by: </span>
      Lyn M
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2030200-bj-rose?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2030200-bj-rose?shelf=contemp-suspense">contemp-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2030200-bj-rose?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74130006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13990407040254385855">The book started out slow, but once the author got all the characters in and established, it started to move along. It was obvious from the beginning that there was a plot against the U.S., and except for Captain Jack, we knew who the 'bad guys' were, and slowly got some of the why. But the purpose, and the actual carrying out of the plot - there were some surprises there. I <i>had</i> to stay up late last night - once the trap was sprung, I couldn't stop.<br/><br/>As with all political thrillers, I find myself </span>
  <span id="freeText13990407040254385855" style="display:none">The book started out slow, but once the author got all the characters in and established, it started to move along. It was obvious from the beginning that there was a plot against the U.S., and except for Captain Jack, we knew who the 'bad guys' were, and slowly got some of the why. But the purpose, and the actual carrying out of the plot - there were some surprises there. I <i>had</i> to stay up late last night - once the trap was sprung, I couldn't stop.<br /><br />As with all political thrillers, I find myself wondering how much has basis in fact and how much is total fabrication (the description of Murder Mountain, for example). I liked the play on names - the leader of the Camel Club is 'Oliver Stone', which we know almost from the beginning is not his real name. The Camel Club is a group of four 'old fogies' who keep an eye on the doings in D.C. - they are fascinating characters, and I will read the next in this series. <br /><br />This wasn't really a 4* read for me because of that very slow start, but much too strong to be just a 3*</span>
  <a data-text-id="13990407040254385855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2701416236" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2701416236" />
    <a title="David Rough" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9801687-david-rough"><img alt="David Rough" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453335151p2/9801687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2701416236?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Rough" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Rough" href="/user/show/9801687-david-rough">David Rough</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2701416236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12443833149638664077">An unusual and unique partnership between Secret Service Agent Alex Ford and four eccentric men called the Camel Club (led by “Oliver Stone”) join together in this novel by David Baldacci, written in 2005. In typical Baldacci flair, this political thriller is laced with adventure and intrigue. The title is aptly spelled with capital “Cs” for CONSPIRACY. I was surprised with a twist toward the end, but being a loyal Buckeye from Ohio I was ahead of the pages on another twisted detail.<br/> <br/>Baldacci in</span>
  <span id="freeText12443833149638664077" style="display:none">An unusual and unique partnership between Secret Service Agent Alex Ford and four eccentric men called the Camel Club (led by “Oliver Stone”) join together in this novel by David Baldacci, written in 2005. In typical Baldacci flair, this political thriller is laced with adventure and intrigue. The title is aptly spelled with capital “Cs” for CONSPIRACY. I was surprised with a twist toward the end, but being a loyal Buckeye from Ohio I was ahead of the pages on another twisted detail.<br /> <br />Baldacci includes this book in his top five novels (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.telegraph.co.uk/books/authors/david-baldacci/my-best-books/">www.telegraph.co.uk/books/authors/dav...</a>). It indeed was a good story with a wide spectrum of special characters, but I am not ready to place in my top five Baldacci offerings. I really enjoyed the John Puller, Amos Decker, and Will Robie books and his sci-fi young adult series, starring Vega Jane, is such good entertainment. This is the first in a series of adventures of The Camel Club and I plan on eavesdropping on the next cover-up very soon. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12443833149638664077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RmHmP9bxTxrGErzMFJpkswaNVK/+aZA5eSDS8xVsWGxP3lk/sPesvdaagO2atmoG9i4RZzTxbSCTxZ12Dv2qeQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2VwedgQ5S9VSnBR1rvEguarbye+RKlaxIMIY7LDUj+LQ46F2Yj+ockIUKFQg3S4MWniMJ1uyq6jKJ1dpq0V99w==')})
  }

In plain truth, Guevara says, “He’s like a kid (James Dean) I went to class with, rode the bus with and slid down an awesome snow-packed hill with.” And after high school, he goes on to Hollywood fame and immortality while Guevara from his modest bookish world is left to wonder about the iconic image, giving it a stark, poignant voice sixty years later. Guevara grew up in Marion, Indiana, where the actor was born. \n\nIn 1954, Dean met perhaps the one real romance of his brief life. Italian actress Pier Angeli was barely 22 when her movie The Silver Chalice coincided with Dean’s East of Eden at Warner Brothers. She’d sneak over to watch him perform, and he would do the same. When they finally interact, Pier’s mother disapproves of Dean’s behavior, attire and not being Catholic.\n\nSome say it was all for the limelight and publicity. Guevara’s gripping and frank story vies otherwise, excavating the actor’s true passion for the lovely but quaint Ms. Angeli.\n\nGuevara is also the author of True Feel, A Circle with Two Corners, and Days of Slint, the first James Dean conceptual novel.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"3928686556630166697\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/9291.David_Baldacci">About David Baldacci</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
